This is not a mistake--we want to give the fused impl\n    # bake-in time before making it the default, even if it is typically faster.\n    if fused is None and foreach is None:\n        _, foreach = _default_to_fused_or_foreach(\n            params, differentiable, use_fused=False\n        )\n        #  284→            &\\textbf{initialize} :  m_0 \\leftarrow 0 \\text{ ( first moment)},\n   285→                v_0\\leftarrow 0 \\text{ (second moment)},\\: v_0^{max}\\leftarrow 0          \\\\[-1.ex]\n   286→            &\\rule{110mm}{0.4pt}                                                                 \\\\\n   287→            &\\textbf{for} \\: t=1 \\: \\textbf{to} \\: \\ldots \\: \\textbf{do}                         \\\\\n   288→\n   289→            &\\hspace{5mm}\\textbf{if} \\: \\textit{maximize}:                                       \\\\\n   290→            &\\hspace{10mm}g_t           \\leftarrow   -\\nabla_{\\theta} f_t (\\theta_{t-1})         \\\\\n   291→            &\\hspace{5mm}\\textbf{else}                                                           \\\\\n   292→            &\\hspace{10mm}g_t           \\leftarrow   \\nabla_{\\theta} f_t (\\theta_{t-1})          \\\\\n   293→            &\\hspace{5mm}\\textbf{if} \\: \\lambda \\neq 0    \\\\\n   299→            &\\hspace{10mm} v_t^{max} \\leftarrow \\mathrm{max}(v_{t-1}^{max},v_t)                  \\\\\n   300→            &\\hspace{10mm}\\widehat{v_t} \\leftarrow                \\big(\\sqrt{\\widehat{v_t}} + \\epsilon \\big)                                       \\\\\n   305→            &\\rule{110mm}{0.4pt}                                                          \\\\[-1.ex]\n   306→            &\\bf{return} \\:  \\theta_t                                                     \\\\[-1.ex]\n   307→            &\\rule{110mm}{0.4pt}                                                          \\\\[-1.ex]\n   308→       \\end{aligned}\n   309→\n   310→    For further details regarding the algorithm we refer to `Adam: A Method for Stochastic Optimization`_.\n   311→    \"\"\"\n   312→    + rf\"\"\"\n   313→    Args:\n   314→        {_params_doc}\n   315→        lr (float, Tensor, optional): learning rate (default: 1e-3). A tensor LR\n   316→            is not yet supported for all our implementations. Please use a float\n   317→            LR if you are not also specifying fused=True or capturable=True.\n   318→        betas (Tuple[float, float], optional): coefficients used for computing\n   319→            running averages of gradient and its square (default: (0.9, 0.999))\n   320→        eps (float, optional): term added to the denominator to improve\n   321→            numerical stability (default: 1e-8)\n   322→        weight_decay (float, optional): weight decay (L2 penalty) (default: 0)\n   323→        decoupled_weight_decay (bool, optional): if True, this optimizer is\n   324→            equivalent to AdamW and the algorithm will not accumulate weight\n   325→            decay in the momentum nor variance. (default: False)\n   326→        amsgrad (bool, optional): whether to use the AMSGrad variant of this\n   327→            algorithm from the paper `On the Convergence of Adam and Beyond`_\n   328→            (default: False)\n   329→        {_foreach_doc}\n   330→        {_maximize_doc}\n   331→        {_capturable_doc}\n   332→        {_differentiable_doc}\n   333→        {_fused_doc}\n   334→    .. Note::\n   335→        A prototype implementation of Adam and AdamW for MPS supports `torch.float32` and `torch.float16`.\n   336→    .. _Adam\\: A Method for Stochastic Optimization:\n   337→        https://arxiv.org/abs/1412.6980\n   338→    .. _On the Convergence of Adam and Beyond:\n   339→        https://openreview.net/forum?id=ryQu7f-RZ\n   340→\n   341→    \"\"\"\n   342→)\n   343→\n   344→\n   345→def _single_tensor_adam(\n   346→    params: list[Tensor],\n   347→    grads: list[Tensor],\n   348→    exp_avgs: list[Tensor],\n   349→    exp_avg_sqs: list[Tensor],\n   350→    max_exp_avg_sqs: list[Tensor],\n   351→    state_steps: list[Tensor],\n   352→    grad_scale: Optional[Tensor],\n   353→    found_inf: Optional[Tensor],\n   354→    *,\n   355→    amsgrad: bool,\n   356→    has_complex: bool,\n   357→    beta1: Union[float, Tensor],\n   358→    beta2: Union[float, Tensor],\n   359→    lr: Union[float, Tensor],\n   360→    weight_decay: float,\n   361→    eps: float,\n   362→    maximize: bool,\n   363→    capturable: bool,\n   364→    differentiable: bool,\n   365→    decoupled_weight_decay: bool,\n   366→):\n   367→    assert grad_scale is None and found_inf is None\n   368→\n   369→    if torch.jit.is_scripting():\n   370→        # TODO: Support nonzero-dim Tensor betas, see #147921\n   379→\n   380→    # We only shuffle around the beta when it is a Tensor, otherwise, we prefer\n   381→    # treating it as a scalar.\n   382→    # Note: ensure type declaration is under conditional check for isinstance\n   383→    # or else torchscript will get cranky about the DeviceDict type.\n   384→    if isinstance(beta1, Tensor):\n   385→        beta1_dict: Optional[DeviceDtypeDict] = {(beta1.device, beta1.dtype): beta1}\n   386→    else:\n   387→        beta1_dict = None\n   388→\n   389→    for i, param in enumerate(params):\n   390→        grad = grads[i] if not maximize else -grads[i]\n   391→        exp_avg = exp_avgs[i]\n   392→        exp_avg_sq = exp_avg_sqs[i]\n   393→        step_t = state_steps[i]\n   394→\n   395→        # If compiling, the compiler will handle cudagraph checks, see note [torch.compile x capturable]\n   396→        if not torch.compiler.is_compiling() and capturable:\n   397→            capturable_supported_devices = _get_capturable_supported_devices()\n   398→            assert (\n   399→                param.device.type == step_t.device.type\n   400→                and param.device.type in capturable_supported_devices\n   401→            ), (\n   402→                f\"If capturable=True, params and state_steps must be on supported devices: {capturable_supported_devices}.\"\n   403→            )\n   404→\n   405→        # update step\n   406→        step_t += 1\n   407→\n   408→        if weight_decay != 0:\n   409→            if decoupled_weight_decay:\n   410→                # Perform stepweight decay\n   411→                param.mul_(1 - lr * weight_decay)\n   412→            else:\n   413→                # Nested if is necessary to bypass jitscript rules\n   414→                if differentiable and isinstance(weight_decay, Tensor):\n   415→                    if weight_decay.requires_grad:\n   416→                        grad = grad.addcmul_(param.clone(), weight_decay)\n   417→                    else:\n   418→                        grad = grad.add(param, alpha=weight_decay)\n   419→                else:\n   420→                    grad = grad.add(param, alpha=weight_decay)\n   421→\n   422→        if torch.is_complex(param):\n   423→            grad = torch.view_as_real(grad)\n   424→            exp_avg = torch.view_as_real(exp_avg)\n   425→            exp_avg_sq = torch.view_as_real(exp_avg_sq)\n   426→            if amsgrad:\n   427→                max_exp_avg_sqs[i] = torch.view_as_real(max_exp_avg_sqs[i])\n   428→            param = torch.view_as_real(param)\n   429→\n   430→        device = param.device\n   431→\n   432→        if beta1_dict is not None:\n   433→            dtype = param.dtype  # Decay the first and second moment running average coefficient\n   447→        exp_avg.lerp_(grad, 1 - device_beta1)\n   448→\n   449→        # Nested if is necessary to bypass jitscript rules\n   450→        if differentiable and isinstance(beta2, Tensor):\n   451→            if beta2.requires_grad:\n   452→                # Using lerp to only use 2 operations bc addcmul's value cannot be a tensor\n   453→                # Showing equivalence of differentiable path and nondifferentiable path\n   454→                # expavg * b2 + grad^2 * (1-b2)\n   455→                #           add expavg * (1-b2) - expavg * (1-b2) = 0\n   456→                # expavg * b2 + expavg * (1-b2) - expavg * (1-b2) + grad^2 * (1-b2)\n   457→                # expavg - expavg * (1-b2) + grad^2 * (1-b2)\n   458→                # expavg + (grad^2 - expavg) * (1-b2)\n   459→                # expavg.lerp(grad^2, 1-beta2)\n   460→                exp_avg_sq.lerp_(torch.square(grad), weight=1 - beta2)\n   461→            else:\n   462→                exp_avg_sq.mul_(beta2).addcmul_(\n   463→                    grad, grad, value=cast(float, 1 - beta2)\n   464→                )\n   465→        else:\n   466→            exp_avg_sq.mul_(beta2).addcmul_(grad, grad, value=1 - beta2)  # Nested if is necessary to bypass jitscript rules\n   481→            if differentiable and isinstance(beta2, Tensor):\n   482→                if beta2.requires_grad:\n   483→                    bias_correction2 = 1 - beta2 ** step.clone()\n   484→                else:\n   485→                    bias_correction2 = 1 - beta2**step\n   486→            else:\n   487→                bias_correction2 = 1 - beta2**step\n   488→\n   489→            step_size = lr / bias_correction1\n   490→            step_size_neg = step_size.neg()\n   491→\n   492→            bias_correction2_sqrt = bias_correction2.sqrt()\n   493→\n   494→            if amsgrad:\n   495→                # Maintains the maximum of all 2nd moment running avg. till now\n   496→                if differentiable:\n   497→                    max_exp_avg_sq = max_exp_avg_sqs[i].clone()\n   498→                else:\n   499→                    max_exp_avg_sq = max_exp_avg_sqs[i]\n   500→\n   501→                max_exp_avg_sqs[i].copy_(torch.maximum(max_exp_avg_sq, exp_avg_sq))\n   502→\n   503→                # Uses the max. for normalizing running avg. of gradient\n   504→                # Folds in (admittedly ugly) 1-elem step_size math here to avoid extra param-set-sized read+write\n   505→                # (can't fold it into addcdiv_ below because addcdiv_ requires value is a Number, not a Tensor)\n   506→                denom = (\n   507→                    max_exp_avg_sqs[i].sqrt() / (bias_correction2_sqrt * step_size_neg)\n   508→                ).add_(eps / step_size_neg)\n   509→            else:\n   510→                denom = (\n   511→                    exp_avg_sq.sqrt() / (bias_correction2_sqrt * step_size_neg)\n   512→                ).add_(eps / step_size_neg)\n   513→\n   514→            if differentiable:\n   515→                param.addcdiv_(exp_avg.clone(), denom)\n   516→            else:\n   517→                param.addcdiv_(exp_avg, denom)\n   518→        else:\n   519→            step = _get_value(step_t)\n   520→\n   521→            bias_correction1 = 1 - beta1**step\n   522→            bias_correction2 = 1 - beta2**step\n   523→\n   524→            step_size = lr / bias_correction1\n   525→\n   526→            bias_correction2_sqrt = bias_correction2**0.5\n   527→\n   528→            if amsgrad:\n   529→                # type: ignore[arg-type]\n   538→\n   539→        # Lastly, switch back to complex view\n   540→        if amsgrad and torch.is_complex(params[i]):\n   541→            max_exp_avg_sqs[i] = torch.view_as_complex(max_exp_avg_sqs[i])\n   542→\n   543→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. \\\\\n\n            &\\hspace{5mm}\\textbf{if} \\: \\textit{maximize}:                                       \\\\\n            &\\hspace{10mm}g_t           \\leftarrow   -\\nabla_{\\theta} f_t (\\theta_{t-1})         \\\\\n            &\\hspace{5mm}\\textbf{else}                                                           \\\\\n            &\\hspace{10mm}g_t           \\leftarrow   \\nabla_{\\theta} f_t (\\theta_{t-1})          \\\\\n            &\\hspace{5mm}\\textbf{if} \\: \\lambda \\neq 0                                           \\\\\n            &\\hspace{10mm} g_t \\leftarrow g_t + \\lambda  \\theta_{t-1}                            \\\\\n            &\\hspace{5mm}m_t           \\leftarrow   \\beta_1 m_{t-1} + (1 - \\beta_1) g_t          \\\\\n            &\\hspace{5mm}v_t           \\leftarrow   \\beta_2 v_{t-1} + (1-\\beta_2) g^2_t          \\\\\n            &\\hspace{5mm}\\widehat{m_t} \\leftarrow   m_t/\\big(1-\\beta_1^t \\big)                   \\\\\n            &\\hspace{5mm}\\textbf{if} \\: amsgrad                                                  \\\\\n            &\\hspace{10mm} v_t^{max} \\leftarrow \\mathrm{max}(v_{t-1}^{max},v_t)                  \\\\\n            &\\hspace{10mm}\\widehat{v_t} \\leftarrow v_t^{max}/\\big(1-\\beta_2^t \\big)              \\\\\n            &\\hspace{5mm}\\textbf{else}                                                           \\\\\n            &\\hspace{10mm}\\widehat{v_t} \\leftarrow   v_t/\\big(1-\\beta_2^t \\big)                  \\\\\n            &\\hspace{5mm}\\theta_t \\leftarrow \\theta_{t-1} - \\gamma \\widehat{m_t}/\n                \\big(\\sqrt{\\widehat{v_t}} + \\epsilon \\big)                                       \\\\\n            &\\rule{110mm}{0.4pt}                                                          \\\\[-1.ex]\n            &\\bf{return} \\:  \\theta_t                                                     \\\\[-1.ex]\n            &\\rule{110mm}{0.4pt}                                                          \\\\[-1.ex]\n       \\end{aligned}\n\n    For further details regarding the algorithm we refer to `Adam: A Method for Stochastic Optimization`_.\n    \"\"\"\n    + rf\"\"\"\n    Args:\n        {_params_doc}\n        lr (float, Tensor, optional): learning rate (default: 1e-3). A tensor LR\n            is not yet supported for all our implementations. Please use a float\n            LR if you are not also specifying fused=True or capturable=True.\n        betas (Tuple[float, float], optional): coefficients used for computing\n            running averages of gradient and its square (default: (0.9, 0.999))\n        eps (float, optional): term added to the denominator to improve\n            numerical stability (default: 1e-8)\n        weight_decay (float, optional): weight decay (L2 penalty) (default: 0)\n        decoupled_weight_decay (bool, optional): if True, this optimizer is\n            equivalent to AdamW and the algorithm will not accumulate weight\n            decay in the momentum nor variance. (default: False)\n        amsgrad (bool, optional): whether to use the AMSGrad variant of this\n            algorithm from the paper `On the Convergence of Adam and Beyond`_\n            (default: False)\n        {_foreach_doc}\n        {_maximize_doc}\n        {_capturable_doc}\n        {_differentiable_doc}\n        {_fused_doc}\n    .. Note::\n        A prototype implementation of Adam and AdamW for MPS supports `torch.float32` and `torch.float16`.\n    .. _Adam\\: A Method for Stochastic Optimization:\n        https://arxiv.org/abs/1412.6980\n    .. _On the Convergence of Adam and Beyond:\n        https://openreview.net/forum?id=ryQu7f-RZ\n\n    \"\"\"\n)\n\n\ndef _single_tensor_adam(\n    params: list[Tensor],\n    grads: list[Tensor],\n    exp_avgs: list[Tensor],\n    exp_avg_sqs: list[Tensor],\n    max_exp_avg_sqs: list[Tensor],\n    state_steps: list[Tensor],\n    grad_scale: Optional[Tensor],\n    found_inf: Optional[Tensor],\n    *,\n    amsgrad: bool,\n    has_complex: bool,\n    beta1: Union[float, Tensor],\n    beta2: Union[float, Tensor],\n    lr: Union[float, Tensor],\n    weight_decay: float,\n    eps: float,\n    maximize: bool,\n    capturable: bool,\n    differentiable: bool,\n    decoupled_weight_decay: bool,\n):\n    assert grad_scale is None and found_inf is None\n\n    if torch.jit.is_scripting():\n        # this assert is due to JIT being dumb and not realizing that the ops below\n        # have overloads to handle both float and Tensor lrs, so we just assert it's\n        # a float since most people using JIT are using floats\n        assert isinstance(lr, float)\n        assert isinstance(beta1, float)\n        assert isinstance(beta2, float)\n    else:\n        lr = _to_scalar(lr)\n        # TODO: Support nonzero-dim Tensor betas, see #147921\n\n    # We only shuffle around the beta when it is a Tensor, otherwise, we prefer\n    # treating it as a scalar.\n    # Note: ensure type declaration is under conditional check for isinstance\n    # or else torchscript will get cranky about the DeviceDict type.\n    if isinstance(beta1, Tensor):\n        beta1_dict: Optional[DeviceDtypeDict] = {(beta1.device, beta1.dtype): beta1}\n    else:\n        beta1_dict = None\n\n    for i, param in enumerate(params):\n        grad = grads[i] if not maximize else -grads[i]\n        exp_avg = exp_avgs[i]\n        exp_avg_sq = exp_avg_sqs[i]\n        step_t = state_steps[i]\n\n        # If compiling, the compiler will handle cudagraph checks, see note [torch.compile x capturable]\n        if not torch.compiler.is_compiling() and capturable:\n            capturable_supported_devices = _get_capturable_supported_devices()\n            assert (\n                param.device.type == step_t.device.type\n                and param.device.type in capturable_supported_devices\n            ), (\n                f\"If capturable=True, params and state_steps must be on supported devices: {capturable_supported_devices}.\"\n            )\n\n        # update step\n        step_t += 1\n\n        if weight_decay != 0:\n            if decoupled_weight_decay:\n                # Perform stepweight decay\n                param.mul_(1 - lr * weight_decay)\n            else:\n                # Nested if is necessary to bypass jitscript rules\n                if differentiable and isinstance(weight_decay, Tensor):\n                    if weight_decay.requires_grad:\n                        grad = grad.addcmul_(param.clone(), weight_decay)\n                    else:\n                        grad = grad.add(param, alpha=weight_decay)\n                else:\n                    grad = grad.add(param, alpha=weight_decay)\n\n        if torch.is_complex(param):\n            grad = torch.view_as_real(grad)\n            exp_avg = torch.view_as_real(exp_avg)\n            exp_avg_sq = torch.view_as_real(exp_avg_sq)\n            if amsgrad:\n                max_exp_avg_sqs[i] = torch.view_as_real(max_exp_avg_sqs[i])\n            param = torch.view_as_real(param)\n\n        device = param.device\n\n        if beta1_dict is not None:\n            dtype = param.dtype  # type: ignore[union-attr]\n\n            # cast to workaround https://github.com/pytorch/pytorch/issues/140601\n            key = (device, dtype)\n            if key not in beta1_dict:\n                beta1_dict[key] = beta1.to(  # type: ignore[union-attr]\n                    device=device, dtype=dtype, non_blocking=True\n                )\n\n            device_beta1: Union[float, Tensor] = beta1_dict[key]\n        else:\n            device_beta1 = beta1\n\n        # Decay the first and second moment running average coefficient\n        exp_avg.lerp_(grad, 1 - device_beta1)\n\n        # Nested if is necessary to bypass jitscript rules\n        if differentiable and isinstance(beta2, Tensor):\n            if beta2.requires_grad:\n                # Using lerp to only use 2 operations bc addcmul's value cannot be a tensor\n                # Showing equivalence of differentiable path and nondifferentiable path\n                # expavg * b2 + grad^2 * (1-b2)\n                #           add expavg * (1-b2) - expavg * (1-b2) = 0\n                # expavg * b2 + expavg * (1-b2) - expavg * (1-b2) + grad^2 * (1-b2)\n                # expavg - expavg * (1-b2) + grad^2 * (1-b2)\n                # expavg + (grad^2 - expavg) * (1-b2)\n                # expavg.lerp(grad^2, 1-beta2)\n                exp_avg_sq.lerp_(torch.square(grad), weight=1 - beta2)\n            else:\n                exp_avg_sq.mul_(beta2).addcmul_(\n                    grad, grad, value=cast(float, 1 - beta2)\n                )\n        else:\n            exp_avg_sq.mul_(beta2).addcmul_(grad, grad, value=1 - beta2)  # type: ignore[arg-type]\n\n        if capturable or differentiable:\n            step = step_t\n\n            # Nested if is necessary to bypass jitscript rules\n            if differentiable and isinstance(beta1, Tensor):\n                if beta1.requires_grad:\n                    bias_correction1 = 1 - beta1 ** step.clone()\n                else:\n                    bias_correction1 = 1 - beta1**step\n            else:\n                bias_correction1 = 1 - beta1**step\n\n            # Nested if is necessary to bypass jitscript rules\n            if differentiable and isinstance(beta2, Tensor):\n                if beta2.requires_grad:\n                    bias_correction2 = 1 - beta2 ** step.clone()\n                else:\n                    bias_correction2 = 1 - beta2**step\n            else:\n                bias_correction2 = 1 - beta2**step\n\n            step_size = lr / bias_correction1\n            step_size_neg = step_size.neg()\n\n            bias_correction2_sqrt = bias_correction2.sqrt()\n\n            if amsgrad:\n                # Maintains the maximum of all 2nd moment running avg. till now\n                if differentiable:\n                    max_exp_avg_sq = max_exp_avg_sqs[i].clone()\n                else:\n                    max_exp_avg_sq = max_exp_avg_sqs[i]\n\n                max_exp_avg_sqs[i].copy_(torch.maximum(max_exp_avg_sq, exp_avg_sq))\n\n                # Uses the max. for normalizing running avg. of gradient\n                # Folds in (admittedly ugly) 1-elem step_size math here to avoid extra param-set-sized read+write\n                # (can't fold it into addcdiv_ below because addcdiv_ requires value is a Number, not a Tensor)\n                denom = (\n                    max_exp_avg_sqs[i].sqrt() / (bias_correction2_sqrt * step_size_neg)\n                ).add_(eps / step_size_neg)\n            else:\n                denom = (\n                    exp_avg_sq.sqrt() / (bias_correction2_sqrt * step_size_neg)\n                ).add_(eps / step_size_neg)\n\n            if differentiable:\n                param.addcdiv_(exp_avg.clone(), denom)\n            else:\n                param.addcdiv_(exp_avg, denom)\n        else:\n            step = _get_value(step_t)\n\n            bias_correction1 = 1 - beta1**step\n            bias_correction2 = 1 - beta2**step\n\n            step_size = lr / bias_correction1\n\n            bias_correction2_sqrt = bias_correction2**0.5\n\n            if amsgrad:\n                # Maintains the maximum of all 2nd moment running avg. till now\n                torch.maximum(max_exp_avg_sqs[i], exp_avg_sq, out=max_exp_avg_sqs[i])\n\n                # Use the max. for normalizing running avg. of gradient\n                denom = (max_exp_avg_sqs[i].sqrt() / bias_correction2_sqrt).add_(eps)\n            else:\n                denom = (exp_avg_sq.sqrt() / bias_correction2_sqrt).add_(eps)\n\n            param.addcdiv_(exp_avg, denom, value=-step_size)  # type: ignore[arg-type]\n\n        # Lastly, switch back to complex view\n        if amsgrad and torch.is_complex(params[i]):\n            max_exp_avg_sqs[i] = torch.view_as_complex(max_exp_avg_sqs[i])\n\n","numLines":543,"startLine":1,"totalLines":974}}}

Detailed Pattern Breakdown: Weight Decay and Maximize Memory Reuse\n\n**Key Optimization Pattern Found in 10 of 11 Optimizers**:\n```python\nif weight_decay != 0:\n    # Reuse the intermediate memory (device_grads) already allocated for maximize\n    if maximize:\n        torch._foreach_add_(device_grads, device_params, alpha=weight_decay)  # in-place\n    else:\n        device_grads = torch._foreach_add(  # new tensor\n            device_grads, device_params, alpha=weight_decay\n        )\n```\n\n**Rationale**: If `maximize=True`, gradients were already negated into a new tensor. After analyzing all 11 optimizers (SGD, Adam, AdaGrad, RMSprop, RAdam, Nadam, AdaMax, AdaDelta, ASGD, RProp, AdaFactor), we found significant code duplication across these functions. Common patterns include:\n\n- Tensor grouping by device and dtype\n- Maximize flag handling (gradient negation)\n- Weight decay with memory reuse optimization\n- State step incrementation\n- Complex tensor handling\n\nThis refactoring will reduce code duplication and make the optimizer implementations more maintainable while preserving backward compatibility.\n\n## Solution Overview\n\nCreate `torch/optim/_foreach.py` with shared helper functions and a higher-level `_foreach_optimizer_step()` orchestrator. This module will extract the common \"boilerplate\" patterns while allowing each optimizer to keep its algorithm-specific logic isolated.\n\n### Strategy: Composition-Based Architecture\n\nInstead of trying to create one monolithic function that handles all cases, we'll provide:\n1. **Helper functions** for each common pattern (e.g., `_handle_maximize()`, `_handle_weight_decay()`)\n2. **Group handling utilities** for device/dtype grouping\n3. **Validation and setup utilities** (empty list check, lr to scalar, complex tensor setup)\n4. **Common gradient/state preprocessing** functions\n\nThis allows optimizers to:\n- Use all helpers if they want, or\n- Mix-and-match helpers for specific patterns, or\n- Implement custom patterns when needed\n\n## Implementation Details\n\n### Files to Create\n1. **`/workspace/torch/optim/_foreach.py`** (NEW)\n   - Helper functions for common patterns\n   - Reusable utility functions\n   - No public API changes\n\n### Files to Modify\n1. **`/workspace/torch/optim/sgd.py`** - Import and use from `_foreach.py`\n2. **`/workspace/torch/optim/adam.py`** - Import and use from `_foreach.py`\n3. **`/workspace/torch/optim/adagrad.py`** - Import and use from `_foreach.py`\n4. (Optional: Others like rmsprop.py, nadam.py, radam.py)\n\n### Module Structure for `_foreach.py`\n\n```python\n# Exports\n__all__ = [\n    \"_foreach_optimizer_step\",  # Main orchestrator (optional)\n    \"handle_maximize\",\n    \"handle_weight_decay\",\n    \"preprocess_state_steps\",\n    \"view_as_real_for_complex\",\n    # ... other helpers as needed\n]\n\n# Functions to extract:\n1. _handle_maximize_grads()\n   - Input: device_grads, maximize flag\n   - Output: modified device_grads (negated if maximize)\n   - Source: Present in all 11 optimizers\n\n2. _handle_weight_decay()\n   - Input: device_grads, device_params, weight_decay, maximize, decoupled_weight_decay\n   - Output: modified device_grads\n   - Source: SGD:419-426, Adam:675-686, AdaGrad:469-476, etc.\n   - Handles memory reuse pattern: reuse negate buffer if maximize=True\n\n3. _increment_state_steps()\n   - Input: device_state_steps\n   - Output: None (in-place modification)\n   - Source: Adam:668-673, AdaGrad:462-467, etc.\n   - Special CPU optimization\n\n4. _prepare_complex_tensors_for_foreach()\n   - Input: has_complex flag, param/grad/state tensors\n   - Output: Same tensors, possibly viewed as real\n   - Source: Adam:645-659, AdaGrad:451-453, etc.\n\n5. _group_by_device_dtype()\n   - Wrapper around Optimizer._group_tensors_by_device_and_dtype()\n   - Input: tensor lists, with_indices flag\n   - Output: grouped tensors dict\n   - Source: Used in all 10 optimizers (except AdaFactor)\n\n# Validation helpers (optional but useful):\n- _validate_params_not_empty() - if len(params) == 0: return\n- _ensure_scalar_lr() - convert tensor lr to scalar\n- _validate_capturable_devices() - for capturable=True optimizers\n```\n\n## Key Design Decisions\n\n1. **No Breaking Changes**: All existing public APIs remain unchanged. The refactoring is internal only.\n\n2. **Composition Over Inheritance**: Rather than inherit from a base class or force a specific pattern, we provide helpers that optimizers can use independently. This preserves the unique structure of each optimizer.\n\n3. **Pattern Reuse, Not Code Duplication**: We extract patterns into named functions that can be called multiple times, making intent clearer.\n\n4. **Gradual Adoption**: Start with 3 optimizers (SGD, Adam, AdaGrad) to validate the approach, then optionally extend to others.\n\n5. **Memory Reuse Pattern**: Particularly important to extract the optimize pattern:\n   ```python\n   if weight_decay != 0:\n       if maximize:\n           torch._foreach_add_(device_grads, ...)  # reuse negated buffer\n       else:\n           device_grads = torch._foreach_add(...)  # create new buffer\n   ```\n\n## Critical Files and Code Locations\n\n### Source Patterns to Extract\n| Pattern | Files | Line Ranges |\n|---------|-------|-----------|\n| Maximize handling | All 11 | Various (e.g., SGD:417, Adam:662, AdaGrad:456) |\n| Weight decay | 10/11 | SGD:419-426, Adam:675-686, AdaGrad:469-476 |\n| State increment | 9/11 | Adam:668-673, AdaGrad:462-467, RMSprop:415-420 |\n| Complex handling | 9/11 | Adam:645-659, AdaGrad:451-453, RMSprop:396-406 |\n| Group by device | 10/11 | SGD:400-410, Adam:613-632, AdaGrad:414-427 |\n\n### Utilities Already Shared (in optimizer.py)\nThese are already imported by all optimizers and should NOT be moved:\n- `_to_scalar()` - `/workspace/torch/optim/optimizer.py:229-245`\n- `_view_as_real()` - `/workspace/torch/optim/optimizer.py:203-208`\n- `_get_value()` - `/workspace/torch/optim/optimizer.py:91-96`\n- `_get_capturable_supported_devices()` - `/workspace/torch/optim/optimizer.py:219-226`\n- `Optimizer._group_tensors_by_device_and_dtype()` - imported from torch.utils._foreach_utils\n\nThese should be leveraged by the new `_foreach.py` module.\n\n## Implementation Steps\n\n1. **Create `/workspace/torch/optim/_foreach.py`**:\n   - Import required utilities from optimizer.py\n   - Define helper functions for common patterns\n   - Keep it well-documented with examples\n\n2. **Update `/workspace/torch/optim/sgd.py`**:\n   - Import helpers from _foreach.py\n   - Replace maximize/weight_decay handling code with calls to helpers\n   - Keep `_multi_tensor_sgd` function signature identical (no breaking changes)\n\n3. **Update `/workspace/torch/optim/adam.py`**:\n   - Similar pattern: import and use helpers\n   - Handle decoupled_weight_decay flag carefully\n   - Keep `_multi_tensor_adam` signature identical\n\n4. **Update `/workspace/torch/optim/adagrad.py`**:\n   - Similar pattern\n   - Preserve sparse gradient fallback logic\n   - Keep `_multi_tensor_adagrad` signature identical\n\n5. **Verification**:\n   - Run existing tests: `python test/test_optim.py::TestOptim::test_foreach_matches_forloop`\n   - Verify no behavior changes (outputs identical to before)\n   - Spot-check code reductions and readability improvements\n\n## Success Criteria\n\n✅ Create `torch/optim/_foreach.py` with at least 4 shared helper functions\n✅ Update at least 3 optimizer files (SGD, Adam, AdaGrad) to import from _foreach\n✅ Eliminate duplicate code for common patterns (maximize, weight_decay, state increment)\n✅ Preserve backward compatibility: all public APIs unchanged\n✅ Pass existing test suite without modifications\n✅ Reduce code duplication across the 3 updated files by at least 20%\n\n## Testing Strategy\n\n1. **No test changes needed** - existing tests should pass unchanged\n2. **Run specific foreach tests**:\n   - `test_foreach_matches_forloop` - validates foreach behavior matches single-tensor\n   - `test_foreach_large_tensor` - memory and performance tests\n   - `test_peak_memory_foreach` - regression in memory usage\n3. **Spot-check**:\n   - SGD with momentum and nesterov\n   - Adam with amsgrad and decoupled_weight_decay\n   - AdaGrad with lr_decay and sparse gradients\n\n## Backward Compatibility Notes\n\n- No public APIs are being changed\n- `_multi_tensor_*` function signatures remain identical\n- Optimizer class constructors and public methods remain unchanged\n- Internal helpers are private (prefixed with `_`)\n- If any optimizer-specific behavior differs post-refactor, immediately revert that file\n\n## Alternative Approaches Considered (Not Chosen)\n\n1. **Create base class for foreach optimizers** - Too rigid, breaks composition\n2. **Extract to `_functional.py`** - Already exists for different purpose (single-tensor implementations)\n3. **Create metaprogramming/decorator solution** - Too complex, hard to debug\n4. **Extract just one function per optimizer** - Doesn't solve the duplication problem\n\nChosen approach (composition-based helpers) provides the best balance of code reuse, readability, and flexibility.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

After analyzing all 11 optimizers (SGD, Adam, AdaGrad, RMSprop, RAdam, Nadam, AdaMax, AdaDelta, ASGD, RProp, AdaFactor), we found significant code duplication across these functions. Common patterns include:\n\n- Tensor grouping by device and dtype\n- Maximize flag handling (gradient negation)\n- Weight decay with memory reuse optimization\n- State step incrementation\n- Complex tensor handling\n\nThis refactoring will reduce code duplication and make the optimizer implementations more maintainable while preserving backward compatibility.\n\n## Solution Overview\n\nCreate `torch/optim/_foreach.py` with shared helper functions and a higher-level `_foreach_optimizer_step()` orchestrator. This module will extract the common \"boilerplate\" patterns while allowing each optimizer to keep its algorithm-specific logic isolated.\n\n### Strategy: Composition-Based Architecture\n\nInstead of trying to create one monolithic function that handles all cases, we'll provide:\n1. **Helper functions** for each common pattern (e.g., `_handle_maximize()`, `_handle_weight_decay()`)\n2. **Group handling utilities** for device/dtype grouping\n3. **Validation and setup utilities** (empty list check, lr to scalar, complex tensor setup)\n4. **Common gradient/state preprocessing** functions\n\nThis allows optimizers to:\n- Use all helpers if they want, or\n- Mix-and-match helpers for specific patterns, or\n- Implement custom patterns when needed\n\n## Implementation Details\n\n### Files to Create\n1. **`/workspace/torch/optim/_foreach.py`** (NEW)\n   - Helper functions for common patterns\n   - Reusable utility functions\n   - No public API changes\n\n### Files to Modify\n1. **`/workspace/torch/optim/sgd.py`** - Import and use from `_foreach.py`\n2. **`/workspace/torch/optim/adam.py`** - Import and use from `_foreach.py`\n3. **`/workspace/torch/optim/adagrad.py`** - Import and use from `_foreach.py`\n4. (Optional: Others like rmsprop.py, nadam.py, radam.py)\n\n### Module Structure for `_foreach.py`\n\n```python\n# Exports\n__all__ = [\n    \"_foreach_optimizer_step\",  # Main orchestrator (optional)\n    \"handle_maximize\",\n    \"handle_weight_decay\",\n    \"preprocess_state_steps\",\n    \"view_as_real_for_complex\",\n    # ... other helpers as needed\n]\n\n# Functions to extract:\n1. _handle_maximize_grads()\n   - Input: device_grads, maximize flag\n   - Output: modified device_grads (negated if maximize)\n   - Source: Present in all 11 optimizers\n\n2. _handle_weight_decay()\n   - Input: device_grads, device_params, weight_decay, maximize, decoupled_weight_decay\n   - Output: modified device_grads\n   - Source: SGD:419-426, Adam:675-686, AdaGrad:469-476, etc.\n   - Handles memory reuse pattern: reuse negate buffer if maximize=True\n\n3. _increment_state_steps()\n   - Input: device_state_steps\n   - Output: None (in-place modification)\n   - Source: Adam:668-673, AdaGrad:462-467, etc.\n   - Special CPU optimization\n\n4. _prepare_complex_tensors_for_foreach()\n   - Input: has_complex flag, param/grad/state tensors\n   - Output: Same tensors, possibly viewed as real\n   - Source: Adam:645-659, AdaGrad:451-453, etc.\n\n5. _group_by_device_dtype()\n   - Wrapper around Optimizer._group_tensors_by_device_and_dtype()\n   - Input: tensor lists, with_indices flag\n   - Output: grouped tensors dict\n   - Source: Used in all 10 optimizers (except AdaFactor)\n\n# Validation helpers (optional but useful):\n- _validate_params_not_empty() - if len(params) == 0: return\n- _ensure_scalar_lr() - convert tensor lr to scalar\n- _validate_capturable_devices() - for capturable=True optimizers\n```\n\n## Key Design Decisions\n\n1. **No Breaking Changes**: All existing public APIs remain unchanged. The refactoring is internal only.\n\n2. **Composition Over Inheritance**: Rather than inherit from a base class or force a specific pattern, we provide helpers that optimizers can use independently. This preserves the unique structure of each optimizer.\n\n3. **Pattern Reuse, Not Code Duplication**: We extract patterns into named functions that can be called multiple times, making intent clearer.\n\n4. **Gradual Adoption**: Start with 3 optimizers (SGD, Adam, AdaGrad) to validate the approach, then optionally extend to others.\n\n5. **Memory Reuse Pattern**: Particularly important to extract the optimize pattern:\n   ```python\n   if weight_decay != 0:\n       if maximize:\n           torch._foreach_add_(device_grads, ...)  # reuse negated buffer\n       else:\n           device_grads = torch._foreach_add(...)  # create new buffer\n   ```\n\n## Critical Files and Code Locations\n\n### Source Patterns to Extract\n| Pattern | Files | Line Ranges |\n|---------|-------|-----------|\n| Maximize handling | All 11 | Various (e.g., SGD:417, Adam:662, AdaGrad:456) |\n| Weight decay | 10/11 | SGD:419-426, Adam:675-686, AdaGrad:469-476 |\n| State increment | 9/11 | Adam:668-673, AdaGrad:462-467, RMSprop:415-420 |\n| Complex handling | 9/11 | Adam:645-659, AdaGrad:451-453, RMSprop:396-406 |\n| Group by device | 10/11 | SGD:400-410, Adam:613-632, AdaGrad:414-427 |\n\n### Utilities Already Shared (in optimizer.py)\nThese are already imported by all optimizers and should NOT be moved:\n- `_to_scalar()` - After analyzing all 11 optimizers (SGD, Adam, AdaGrad, RMSprop, RAdam, Nadam, AdaMax, AdaDelta, ASGD, RProp, AdaFactor), we found significant code duplication across these functions. Common patterns include:\n\n- Tensor grouping by device and dtype\n- Maximize flag handling (gradient negation)\n- Weight decay with memory reuse optimization\n- State step incrementation\n- Complex tensor handling\n\nThis refactoring will reduce code duplication and make the optimizer implementations more maintainable while preserving backward compatibility.\n\n## Solution Overview\n\nCreate `torch/optim/_foreach.py` with shared helper functions and a higher-level `_foreach_optimizer_step()` orchestrator. This module will extract the common \"boilerplate\" patterns while allowing each optimizer to keep its algorithm-specific logic isolated.\n\n### Strategy: Composition-Based Architecture\n\nInstead of trying to create one monolithic function that handles all cases, we'll provide:\n1. **Helper functions** for each common pattern (e.g., `_handle_maximize()`, `_handle_weight_decay()`)\n2. **Group handling utilities** for device/dtype grouping\n3. **Validation and setup utilities** (empty list check, lr to scalar, complex tensor setup)\n4. **Common gradient/state preprocessing** functions\n\nThis allows optimizers to:\n- Use all helpers if they want, or\n- Mix-and-match helpers for specific patterns, or\n- Implement custom patterns when needed\n\n## Implementation Details\n\n### Files to Create\n1. **`/workspace/torch/optim/_foreach.py`** (NEW)\n   - Helper functions for common patterns\n   - Reusable utility functions\n   - No public API changes\n\n### Files to Modify\n1. **`/workspace/torch/optim/sgd.py`** - Import and use from `_foreach.py`\n2. **`/workspace/torch/optim/adam.py`** - Import and use from `_foreach.py`\n3. **`/workspace/torch/optim/adagrad.py`** - Import and use from `_foreach.py`\n4. (Optional: Others like rmsprop.py, nadam.py, radam.py)\n\n### Module Structure for `_foreach.py`\n\n```python\n# Exports\n__all__ = [\n    \"_foreach_optimizer_step\",  # Main orchestrator (optional)\n    \"handle_maximize\",\n    \"handle_weight_decay\",\n    \"preprocess_state_steps\",\n    \"view_as_real_for_complex\",\n    # ... other helpers as needed\n]\n\n# Functions to extract:\n1. _handle_maximize_grads()\n   - Input: device_grads, maximize flag\n   - Output: modified device_grads (negated if maximize)\n   - Source: Present in all 11 optimizers\n\n2. _handle_weight_decay()\n   - Input: device_grads, device_params, weight_decay, maximize, decoupled_weight_decay\n   - Output: modified device_grads\n   - Source: SGD:419-426, Adam:675-686, AdaGrad:469-476, etc.\n   - Handles memory reuse pattern: reuse negate buffer if maximize=True\n\n3. _increment_state_steps()\n   - Input: device_state_steps\n   - Output: None (in-place modification)\n   - Source: Adam:668-673, AdaGrad:462-467, etc.\n   - Special CPU optimization\n\n4. _prepare_complex_tensors_for_foreach()\n   - Input: has_complex flag, param/grad/state tensors\n   - Output: Same tensors, possibly viewed as real\n   - Source: Adam:645-659, AdaGrad:451-453, etc.\n\n5. _group_by_device_dtype()\n   - Wrapper around Optimizer._group_tensors_by_device_and_dtype()\n   - Input: tensor lists, with_indices flag\n   - Output: grouped tensors dict\n   - Source: Used in all 10 optimizers (except AdaFactor)\n\n# Validation helpers (optional but useful):\n- _validate_params_not_empty() - if len(params) == 0: return\n- _ensure_scalar_lr() - convert tensor lr to scalar\n- _validate_capturable_devices() - for capturable=True optimizers\n```\n\n## Key Design Decisions\n\n1. **No Breaking Changes**: All existing public APIs remain unchanged. The refactoring is internal only.\n\n2. **Composition Over Inheritance**: Rather than inherit from a base class or force a specific pattern, we provide helpers that optimizers can use independently. This preserves the unique structure of each optimizer.\n\n3. **Pattern Reuse, Not Code Duplication**: We extract patterns into named functions that can be called multiple times, making intent clearer.\n\n4. **Gradual Adoption**: Start with 3 optimizers (SGD, Adam, AdaGrad) to validate the approach, then optionally extend to others.\n\n5. **Memory Reuse Pattern**: Particularly important to extract the optimize pattern:\n   ```python\n   if weight_decay != 0:\n       if maximize:\n           torch._foreach_add_(device_grads, ...)  # reuse negated buffer\n       else:\n           device_grads = torch._foreach_add(...)  # create new buffer\n   ```\n\n## Critical Files and Code Locations\n\n### Source Patterns to Extract\n| Pattern | Files | Line Ranges |\n|---------|-------|-----------|\n| Maximize handling | All 11 | Various (e.g., SGD:417, Adam:662, AdaGrad:456) |\n| Weight decay | 10/11 | SGD:419-426, Adam:675-686, AdaGrad:469-476 |\n| State increment | 9/11 | Adam:668-673, AdaGrad:462-467, RMSprop:415-420 |\n| Complex handling | 9/11 | Adam:645-659, AdaGrad:451-453, RMSprop:396-406 |\n| Group by device | 10/11 | SGD:400-410, Adam:613-632, AdaGrad:414-427 |\n\n### Utilities Already Shared (in optimizer.py)\nThese are already imported by all optimizers and should NOT be moved:\n- `_to_scalar()` - `/workspace/torch/optim/optimizer.py:219-226`\n- `Optimizer._group_tensors_by_device_and_dtype()` - imported from torch.utils._foreach_utils\n\nThese should be leveraged by the new `_foreach.py` module.\n\n## Implementation Steps\n\n1. **Create `/workspace/torch/optim/_foreach.py`**:\n   -
